                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=High+Entropy&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_high%20entropy">high entropy</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=High+Working+Voltage&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_high%20working%20voltage">high working voltage</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Potassium+Hexacyanoferrate&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_potassium%20hexacyanoferrate">potassium hexacyanoferrate</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Cathode&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_cathode">cathode</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium+Ion+Batteries&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_sodium%20ion%20batteries">sodium ion batteries</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody" style="width: 384px;"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="NLM_p first">Sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have been demonstrated as a promising alternative to conventional lithium ion batteries (LIBs) because of their low cost, wider distribution in the earth’s crust, and similar chemical properties to LIBs. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4 ref5 ref6" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4 ref5 ref6" aria-label="reference 1 to 6">(1−6)</a> However, the large volume change of the electrode during Na<sup>+</sup> insertion/extraction, sluggish Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics, low operating voltage, and unsatisfactory energy density of cathode materials prevent their practical application. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref7 ref8 ref9" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref7 ref8 ref9" aria-label="reference 7 to 9">(7−9)</a> The cathode material is the crucial part in SIB, the commonly available materials mainly include polyanionic compounds, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref10 ref11" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref10 ref11" aria-label="reference 10 and 11">(10,11)</a> layered oxides, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref12 ref13 ref14 ref15 ref16 ref17" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref12 ref13 ref14 ref15 ref16 ref17" aria-label="reference 12 to 17">(12−17)</a> and Prussian blue analogues (PBAs). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9 ref18 ref19 ref20 ref21 ref22" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref9 ref18 ref19 ref20 ref21 ref22" aria-label="reference 9 and 18 to 22">(9,18−22)</a> Among these cathode candidates, PBAs are the most promising cathodes due to the irreplaceable advantages, such as open three-dimensional ion channels to achieve stable rapid Na<sup>+</sup> (de)intercalation and an environmentally friendly synthesis process for further large-scale production. The chemical formula of PBAs can be summarized as A<sub><i>x</i></sub>M<sub>1</sub>[M<sub>2</sub>(CN)<sub>6</sub>]<sub>1–<i>y</i></sub>·□<sub><i>y</i></sub>·<i>n</i>H<sub>2</sub>O (0 ≤ <i>x</i> ≤ 2, 0 ≤ <i>y</i> &lt; 1, A: alkali metal ions, M<sub>1/2</sub>: transition metals, □: vacancies). In general, the carbon-coordinated M<sub>2</sub> site is occupied by Fe, while the nitrogen-coordinated M<sub>1</sub> site can be occupied by multiple transition metal elements, such as Mn, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref23" aria-label="reference 23">(23)</a> Fe, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref9" aria-label="reference 9">(9)</a> Co, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref24" aria-label="reference 24">(24)</a> Ni, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref25" aria-label="reference 25">(25)</a> Cu, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref26" aria-label="reference 26">(26)</a> etc. In consideration of energy density and economy of SIBs, the M<sub>1</sub> site in the crystalline structure is most likely occupied by Mn because of its high average voltage and high abundance, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref27 ref28" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref27 ref28" aria-label="reference 27 and 28">(27,28)</a> while the Jahn–Teller distortions will result in crystal structure damage and fast capacity decay of battery. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29 ref30" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref29 ref30" aria-label="reference 29 and 30">(29,30)</a> Despite strategies that partially replacing Mn with other transition metal elements (i.e., Fe, Ni, Co, and Cu) have been used to improve the structure stability of PBAs, the individual cation doping may trigger the materials compositional disorder and structural rearrangements issues, which is hardly to achieve satisfactory long-term cycle stability of SIBs. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref31 ref32 ref33 ref34" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref31 ref32 ref33 ref34" aria-label="reference 31 to 34">(31−34)</a> Therefore, it is highly desirable to develop more effective strategies for stabilizing the electrode structure to boost advanced SIBs with a high energy density and superior long-term stability.</div><div class="NLM_p">Recently, the effect of high entropy in various materials has received increased attention because of their interesting “Cocktail Effect” and high potential for tailored energy storage properties. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref10 ref35 ref36 ref37 ref38 ref39" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref10 ref35 ref36 ref37 ref38 ref39" aria-label="reference 10 and 35 to 39">(10,35−39)</a> Researchers have employed high-entropy layered oxides or high-entropy metal–organic framework structures as cathodes for SIBs, obtaining enhanced sodium storage performances due to the entropy stabilization actions. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref35 ref36 ref37 ref38 ref39" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref35 ref36 ref37 ref38 ref39" aria-label="reference 35 to 39">(35−39)</a> However, the introduction of multiple transition metal species in the high-entropy cathode would undoubtedly weaken the average voltage, thus reducing the energy density of SIBs. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref37 ref38" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref37 ref38" aria-label="reference 37 and 38">(37,38)</a> It will be very challenging but highly profitable to simultaneously improve the cycling stability and maintain high voltage platform of SIBs. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref39" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref39" aria-label="reference 39">(39)</a> Interestingly, it is reported that PBA cathode host prefers to bond with K<sup>+</sup> rather than Na<sup>+</sup> compared with polyanionic compounds and layered oxides even though K<sup>+</sup> (1.38 Å) has a lager radius than that of Na<sup>+</sup> (1.02 Å). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref40 ref41 ref42" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref40 ref41 ref42" aria-label="reference 40 to 42">(40−42)</a> Therefore, the replacement of Na with K in the PBA cathode structure may possibly increase the structural stability. Meanwhile, it can also push the working voltage to higher potential region because of lower redox potential of K<sup>+</sup>/K (−2.93 V vs. SHE) than that of Na<sup>+</sup>/Na (−2.71 V vs SHE). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref43" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref43" aria-label="reference 43">(43)</a> One can expect that the good sodium storage performance of PBAs can be reached via combining the strategies of high-entropy and replacing Na with K in PBAs crystal.</div><div class="NLM_p last">Herein, we propose the high-entropy and potassium incorporation strategy to fabricate the K<sub><i>x</i></sub>(MnFeCoNiCu)[Fe(CN)<sub>6</sub>] (denoted as HE-K-PBA) cathode via a facile coprecipitation method for SIBs, in which five transition metal elements (Mn, Fe, Co, Ni and Cu) occupy M<sub>1</sub> site in equimolarly, and potassium ions completely enter A site. The everlasting (de)intercalation of K<sup>+</sup> in the high entropy frame endows the HE-K-PBA cathode with a stable high voltage plateau (3.46 V) and superior cycling stability (90.4% of capacity retention after 1700 cycles at 1.0 A g<sup>–1</sup>). And the full-cell with the HE-K-PBA cathode and hard carbon anode can exhibit a high reversible capacity of 182.4 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 1.0 A g<sup>–1</sup> after 200 cycles. In addition, when used as a cathode for all-solid-state battery, the HE-K-PBA can deliver a stable median voltage of 3.29 V over 3000 cycles. In addition, the reaction mechanism of variable valence states of elements and intrinsic structure stability for the HE-K-PBA cathode are systematically investigated by combining in/ex situ characterization and theoretical simulations.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">Results and Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">The crystal structure of HE-K-PBA is depicted in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>a. Obviously, five cations (Mn, Fe, Co, Ni, and Cu) with equal mole ratios occupy uniformly at the nitrogen-coordinated position. The carbon-coordinated position is occupied by low spin Fe, which forms the three-dimensional framework of HE-K-PBA. To verify the high entropy structure, synchrotron radiation X-ray absorption spectroscopy (XAS) was performed to characterize the coordination environment around each transition metal cation. The homologous extended X-ray absorption fine structure (EXAFS) curves were rendered in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>b. Clearly, the curve distribution of each transition metal cation is very similar, indicating that the coordination environment around each metal cation is consistent. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref37 ref38" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref37 ref38" aria-label="reference 37 and 38">(37,38)</a> As previously reported, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref37 ref38" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref37 ref38" aria-label="reference 37 and 38">(37,38)</a> two dominant peaks can be attributed to M-N and M-C shells, respectively. Compared with other spectra, it should be noted that there is a slight variation for the Fe K-edge after Fourier transform, which can be assigned to the stretching of Fe–C≡N. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref37 ref38" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref37 ref38" aria-label="reference 37 and 38">(37,38)</a> The crystal structure of HE-K-PBA was examined by X-ray diffraction (XRD) and the corresponding Rietveld refinement curves (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>c), demonstrating a monoclinic phase (<i>P</i>2<sub>1</sub>/<i>n</i> space group, <i>a</i> = 10.0900 Å, <i>b</i> = 7.2620 Å, <i>c</i> = 7.0030 Å, α = γ = 90°, β = 89.66°). Detailed atomic positions are listed in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S1</a>, indicating that the five nitrogen-coordinated metal cations occupy the 2d site uniformly. As a contrast, the Mn-based PBA (K<sub><i>x</i></sub>Mn[Fe(CN)<sub>6</sub>], termed Mn-K-PBA) cathode was synthesized. The X-ray diffraction (XRD) and the corresponding Rietveld refinement curves of Mn-K-PBA are shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S1</a>, demonstrating a monoclinic phase (P2<sub>1</sub>/n space group, <i>a</i> = 10.10970 Å, <i>b</i> = 7.34029 Å, <i>c</i> = 6.96364 Å, α = γ = 90°, β = 90.2646°). Detailed atomic positions are listed in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S2</a>. The morphologies of HE-K-PBA and Mn-K-PBA cathodes are detected by the transmission electron microscopy (TEM) images (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>d and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2</a>), which exhibit similar uniform small particles (size: ∼50 nm). According to high resolution TEM (HRTEM) images of HE-K-PBA, uniform lattice fringes appear on the particle, and the lattice spacing is 0.35 nm, which can be indexed as (220) crystal planes (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>e). <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>f and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3</a> show the scanning TEM (STEM) images and energy dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDS), clearly confirming that five transition metal elements are equally distributed within the HE-K-PBA particles. The STEM image and corresponding EDS of Mn-K-PBA also suggest the good dispersion of Mn in the host, as illustrated in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S4</a>. According to X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) analysis of HE-K-PBA (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S5 and S6</a>), potassium ions and five transition metal ions are captured in HE-K-PBA, among which copper exists in the form of Cu<sup>+/2+</sup>, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26 ref44" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref26 ref44" aria-label="reference 26 and 44">(26,44)</a> cobalt exists as Co<sup>2+/3+</sup>, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref45 ref46" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref45 ref46" aria-label="reference 45 and 46">(45,46)</a> and other three transition metal cations are divalent. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref47 ref48" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref47 ref48" aria-label="reference 47 and 48">(47,48)</a> The XPS spectra of Mn-K-PBA are displayed in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S7 and S8</a>, which illustrates the presence of K<sup>+</sup>, Mn<sup>2+</sup> and Fe<sup>2+</sup>. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref47 ref48" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref47 ref48" aria-label="reference 47 and 48">(47,48)</a> The Raman spectra were used to investigated the vibration stretching mode of C≡N <sup>̵</sup>to further reflect the chemical environment of each cation (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S9</a>). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28 ref48 ref49" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref28 ref48 ref49" aria-label="reference 28, 48 and 49">(28,48,49)</a> Obviously, both HE-K-PBA and Mn-K-PBA exhibit two vibration peaks (2083 and 2124 cm<sup>–1</sup> for HE-K-PBA, 2076 and 2116 cm<sup>–1</sup> for Mn-K-PBA, respectively), indicating that the iron cations in carbon coordination exhibit Fe<sup>2+</sup>, while the nitrogen coordinated cations exhibit M<sup>2+/3+</sup> and Mn<sup>2+/3+</sup>, respectively. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28 ref49" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref28 ref49" aria-label="reference 28 and 49">(28,49)</a> Crystal water content of PBAs is an important parameter, because it can affect the electrochemical performance of batteries. The crystal water content in the HE-K-PBA and Mn-K-PBA skeletons were estimated by thermogravimetric analyzer (TGA), and the contents of absorbed water and interstitial water were distinguished by the curves (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S10</a>). Apparently, the interstitial water contents of HE-K-PBA and Mn-K-PBA cathodes are 2.099% and 2.472%, respectively, which is beneficial to the long-term cycling stability of HE-K-PBA cathode. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref27 ref32" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref27 ref32" aria-label="reference 27 and 32">(27,32)</a> In virtue of inductively coupled plasma-optical emission spectroscopy (ICP-OES) analysis, the molecular formula of HE-K-PBA is determined to be K<sub>1.29</sub>Mn<sub>0.2</sub>Fe<sub>0.2</sub>Co<sub>0.21</sub>Ni<sub>0.19</sub>Cu<sub>0.21</sub>[Fe(CN)]<sub>0.85</sub>·0.39H<sub>2</sub>O (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S3</a>).</div><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/asset/images/medium/nn3c02323_0001.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/asset/images/large/nn3c02323_0001.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. (a) Schematic crystal structure of HE-K-PBA. (b) Extended X-ray absorption fine structure (EXAFS) signals of five transition metal of HE-K-PBA. (c) XRD pattern and corresponding Rietveld refinement plot of HE-K-PBA. (d) TEM image and (e) HRTEM images of HE-K-PBA. (f) STEM image and EDS mapping images of HE-K-PBA.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/asset/images/large/nn3c02323_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.3c02323&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">Combining the merits of high-entropy and potassium incorporation, the HE-K-PBA cathode is expected to simultaneously deliver good cycling stability and high output voltage, which are verified by systematic electrochemical measurements in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>. The HE-K-PBA shows a high discharge specific capacity (120.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>) and energy density (400.4 Wh kg<sup>–1</sup>) with high initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) of 91% at 0.01 A g<sup>–1</sup> and a smaller polarization–voltage of 0.145 V in the voltage window of 2.0–4.2 V (vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na) which outweigh those of Mn-K-PBA (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>a and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S11a</a>). The good electrochemical reversibility of HE-K-PBA was investigated by cyclic voltammetry (CV) plots, shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>b. HE-K-PBA displays a distinct symmetric pair of redox peaks at 3.59 V/3.46 V and highly reversible electrochemical process. And for Mn-K-PBA (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S11b</a>), two pairs of redox peaks at 3.71/3.59 V and 3.60/3.44 V can be observed, corresponding to the nitrogen-coordinated Mn<sup>2+/3+</sup> and carbon-coordinated low spin Fe<sup>2+/3+</sup> redox couples, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30 ref43" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref30 ref43" aria-label="reference 30 and 43">(30,43)</a> respectively. The insufficient activation of low spin Fe<sup>2+/3+</sup> redox and Jahn–Teller distortions caused by the nitrogen-coordination of Mn<sup>2+/3+</sup> result in the poor reversibility and severe capacity decay of the Mn-K-PBA, which can also be seen from the rapid strength weakening of the two pairs of redox peaks in the Mn-K-PBA. The rate performance of HE-K-PBA and Mn-K-PBA are compared and presented in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>c and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S12</a>. HE-K-PBA exhibits high reversible capacities of 110.3, 100.5, 90.2, 83.7, 76.0, 69.0, 65.7, 60.0, and 56.0 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.05, 0.1, 0.2, 0.3, 0.5, 0.8, 1.0, 1.5, and 2.0 A g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively, while Mn-K-PBA shows poorer performance than that of the HE-K-PBA due to the superior electrochemical kinetics and structure stability of HE-K-PBA. <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S13</a> compares the median voltages of HE-K-PBA and Mn-K-PBA at different current densities, which is crucial for the energy density of batteries. The median voltage of Mn-K-PBA cathode is 3.51 V at 0.01 A g<sup>–1</sup>, which is higher than that of HE-K-PBA. However, with the increasing of current density, the median voltage of Mn-K-PBA cathode decreases rapidly, indicating the Jahn–Teller distortions of Mn-K-PBA can interfere with the normal electrochemical equilibrium seriously. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref50" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref50" aria-label="reference 50">(50)</a> In contrast, the median voltage of HE-K-PBA decreases slowly even at a high rate, demonstrating the good structure stability of HE-K-PBA.</div><figure id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/asset/images/medium/nn3c02323_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/asset/images/large/nn3c02323_0002.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. (a) Galvanostatic charge/discharge curves at 0.01 A g<sup>–1</sup> of the first three cycles. (b) CV curves of first three cycles at 0.05 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. (c) Rate performance of HE-K-PBA and Mn-K-PBA. (d) Linear fitting Randles-Sevcik curves by plotting the maximal current as a function of the square root of the sweep rate. (e) Arrhenius plots and corresponding activation energy of HE-K-PBA and Mn-K-PBA. (f) Cycling performance of HE-K-PBA and Mn-K-PBA at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>, (the inset figure provides the enlarged view of corresponding Coulombic efficiency). (g) Long-term cycling performance of HE-K-PBA and Mn-K-PBA at 1.0 A g<sup>–1</sup>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/asset/images/large/nn3c02323_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.3c02323&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">To investigate the electrochemical kinetics of HE-K-PBA and Mn-K-PBA, we measured the ion diffusion coefficient (<i>D</i>) was measured. The <i>D</i> can be calculated by performing CV measurements with continually increased sweep rates (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S14</a>) and the Randles-Sevcik eq (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#eqS1" aria-label="eq 1">eq 1</a>, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>) by plotting the maximal current as a function of the square root of the sweep rate (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>d and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S4</a>). HE-K-PBA exhibits higher D values both in the deintercalation and intercalation processes than those of the Mn-K-PBA, indicating good reaction kinetics of HE-K-PBA. Furthermore, the kinetics can be fundamentally represented by the activation energy (<i>E</i><sub>a</sub>) from Arrhenius equation. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref51" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref51" aria-label="reference 51">(51)</a> <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>e exhibits the Arrhenius plots and the corresponding <i>E</i><sub>a</sub> of HE-K-PBA and Mn-K-PBA (variable temperature impedance curves are shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S15</a>). The <i>E</i><sub>a</sub> of HE-K-PBA (54.4 kJ mol<sup>–1</sup>) is lower than that of Mn-K-PBA (62.5 kJ mol<sup>–1</sup>), further demonstrating the superior kinetics of HE-K-PBA for sodium storage. In addition, we also investigated the electrochemical kinetics of HE-K-PBA and Mn-K-PBA after 100 cycles (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S16</a>). Obviously, the electrochemical kinetics of HE-K-PBA is still better than those of Mn-K-PBA after cycles. Benefiting from the stable electrode structure and fast reaction kinetics,  HE-K-PBA delivers good long-term cycling stability. As shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>f and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S17</a>, HE-K-PBA displays a high initial discharge capacity of 100 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> with a capacity retention of 82.8% after 300 cycles at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup> while Mn-K-PBA only presents initial capacity of 61.7 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> with low capacity retention of 38.7%. According to the inset figure in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>f, the HE-K-PBA cathode shows a much higher Coulombic efficiency (above 99%) than that of the Mn-K-PBA during 300 cycles, which suggests HE-K-PBA effectively mitigates the Jahn–Teller effect and maintains the structure stability. Even at high current density of 1.0 A g<sup>–1</sup>, the HE-K-PBA delivers high reversible capacity of 64.0 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after activation, and achieves ultrahigh retention of 90.4% after 1700 cycles (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>g). All the above results prove that the introduction of a high-entropy structure can enhance the electrochemical kinetics and cycling stability of SIBs. Additionally, in order to meet the requirement of the practical application, the electrode with higher mass loading (6 mg cm<sup>–2</sup>) was fabricated, which can deliver high specific capacity of 91.4 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> with 85.7% capacity retention over 120 cycles at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>as shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S18</a>.</div><div class="NLM_p">The influence of potassium incorporation in the high-entropy framework on the long-term median voltage of HE-K-PBA is verified via electrochemical tests. As presented in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>a, only one pair of main redox peaks can be seen in the CV curves of HE-Na-PBA and HE-K-PBA. Both oxidation peak and reduction peak of HE-K-PBA are significantly higher than those of the HE-Na-PBA. For instance, the reduction peak voltage of HE-K-PBA cathode is 3.46 V, which is 0.2 V higher than that of the HE-Na-PBA cathode. The stability of median voltage during the long cycling process is further evaluated for HE-K-PBA and HE-Na-PBA cathodes at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup> in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>b. Apparently, a stable voltage gap can be observed between HE-K-PBA and HE-Na-PBA during the 300 continuous 300 cycles. The long-term cycling performance and rate performance of  HE-Na-PBA are shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S19</a>. The normalized charge–discharge curves exhibit clearly stable voltage lifting of HE-K-PBA at different cycle numbers (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S20</a>), confirming that the introduction of potassium in the high-entropy cathode can steadily maintain a high voltage platform of HE-K-PBA. The (de)intercalation mechanism of potassium in the HE-K-PBA is elucidated by <i>ex situ</i> XRD as exhibited in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S21</a>. The phase of HE-K-PBA at different states corresponds perfectly to the original state even after 300 cycles, while the (de)intercalation of Na<sup>+</sup> not occurred in the HE-K-PBA during the long-term electrochemical cycling, suggesting K<sup>+</sup> can be capable of reversible (de)intercalation in the HE-K-PBA with negligible consumption. Additionally, the phase of HE-K-PBA remained unchanged after 300 cycles, indicating its good structural stability. Herein, we compared the medium discharge voltage of HE-K-PBA with other reported cathode materials for SIBs, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9 ref15 ref24 ref25 ref26 ref27 ref35 ref38 ref39 ref52 ref53 ref54 ref55" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref9 ref15 ref24 ref25 ref26 ref27 ref35 ref38 ref39 ref52 ref53 ref54 ref55" aria-label="reference 9, 15, 24 to 27, 35, 38, 39 and 52 to 55">(9,15,24−27,35,38,39,52−55)</a> and the HE-K-PBA cathodes exhibit a highly competitive discharge voltage (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>c), indicating its huge potential for developing high energy density SIBs.</div><figure id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/asset/images/medium/nn3c02323_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/asset/images/large/nn3c02323_0003.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. (a) First CV curves of HE-K-PBA and HE-Na-PBA at 0.05 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. (b) Long-term median voltage performance of HE-K-PBA and HE-Na-PBA at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>. (c) Comparison of medium discharge voltages of the HE-K-PBA electrodes with other as-reported cathodes for SIBs. (d) <i>Ex situ</i> XPS analysis and (e) <i>ex situ</i> TOF-SIMS analysis of HE-K-PBA cathode during the second cycle. (f) <i>In situ</i> Raman spectra analysis. (g) <i>Ex situ</i> normalized XANES spectra at the Mn, Fe, Co, Ni, and Cu K-edges of the HE-K-PBA cathode with original, full charge, and full discharge state.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/asset/images/large/nn3c02323_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.3c02323&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">To better understand the electrochemical behavior during the charge and discharge process, <i>ex situ</i> XPS analysis was examined on HE-K-PBA electrodes after charge and discharge (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>d and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S22</a>). The K<sup>+</sup> peak intensity decreases gradually during the charging process, and finally disappearing at the fully charged state (4.2 V), showing the extraction of K<sup>+</sup> from the HE-K-PBA cathode. And the K<sup>+</sup> peak intensity gradually increases during the discharging process to 2 V, implying the insertion of K<sup>+</sup> into the lattice. In addition, <i>ex situ</i> time-of-flight secondary ion mass spectrometry (TOF-SIMS) analysis was examined to observe the (de)intercalation of K<sup>+</sup> more visually (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>e). In <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S23a</a>, the initial state HE-K-PBA electrode exhibits an obvious K<sup>+</sup> signal. Apparently, during the second charge/discharge cycle, the K<sup>+</sup> signal is weak in the fully charged state. And at the fully discharged state, the signal of K<sup>+</sup> returns to a strong state. This significant contrast is still evident after 10 cycles (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S23b and c</a>), which indicates that K<sup>+</sup> can stably (de)intercalate from the HE-K-PBA during cycling. Furthermore, in order to prove the long-term stability of K<sup>+</sup> (de)intercalation in the HE-K-PBA cathode, the XPS analysis after 300 cycles was applied in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S24</a>. Apparently, the K<sup>+</sup> peak intensity is weak at 4.2 V and recovers strong signal at 2 V, showing highly reversible of (de)intercalation behavior of K<sup>+</sup> in the HE-K-PBA cathode.</div><div class="NLM_p">To further investigate the ion (de)intercalation behaviors during the charge/discharge process, the cells assembled with copper foil as anode and HE-K-PBA as cathode were prepared. When the cells were charged to 4.2 V under different current densities, the high-angle annular dark-field scanning TEM (HAADF STEM) and energy dispersive X-ray spectroscopy of the anodes were examined as shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S25 and S26</a>. Obvious Na<sup>+</sup> signals can be observed in the copper foil anodes without K<sup>+</sup> deposition signals. And the selected-area electron diffraction (SAED) in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S27</a> also shows the Na and NaO<sub>2</sub> species while no K species could be captured, which is well consistent with the results of SEM micrograph and corresponding EDS mapping analysis <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S28 and S29</a>. All these results suggest that Na ions intercalate the anode when K ions are deintercalated from the HE-K-PBA. In addition, we also investigated the (de)intercalation mechanism in the Mn-K-PBA cathode by <i>ex situ</i> XRD as exhibited in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S30</a>. The phase transition of Mn-K-PBA can be observed at the 50th cycle and become obviously at the 100th cycle, suggesting that Na<sup>+</sup> will gradually replace K<sup>+</sup> in Mn-K-PBA cathode during the cycling process. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref30" aria-label="reference 30">(30)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">In consideration of the high sensitivity of the (C≡N)<sup>−</sup> vibration stretching mode to the chemical coordination environment of bonding iron and M (M: Mn, Fe, Co, Ni, Cu), <i>in situ</i> Raman spectroscopy was performed to reveal the reaction mechanism of the HE-K-PBA in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>f. At the initial state, the Raman spectrum presents two strong peaks located at 2085 and 2125 cm<sup>–1</sup>, which can be attributed to the Fe<sup>2+</sup>-C≡N-M<sup>2+</sup> and Fe<sup>2+</sup>-C≡N-M<sup>3+</sup> groups, respectively. As the charging process progressed, the peak at 2080 cm<sup>–1</sup> gradually disappears, which can be indexed as the Fe<sup>2+</sup>-C≡N-M<sup>2+</sup> group oxidized to Fe<sup>2+</sup>-C≡N-M<sup>3+</sup> groups. At the fully charged state (charged to 4.2 V), the peak at 2125 cm<sup>–1</sup> disappears and only exists a peak at 2165 cm<sup>–1</sup>, indicating that all the Fe<sup>2+</sup>-C≡N-M<sup>3+</sup> group is oxidized to Fe<sup>3+</sup>-C≡N-M<sup>3+</sup> groups. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28 ref48 ref49 ref56" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref28 ref48 ref49 ref56" aria-label="reference 28, 48, 49 and 56">(28,48,49,56)</a> In the subsequent discharge process from 4.2  to 2 V, the peak at 2164 cm<sup>–1</sup> disappears and the initial two peaks at 2085 and 2125 cm<sup>–1</sup> appear, indicating highly reversible reactions of HE-K-PBA during electrochemical cycling.</div><div class="NLM_p">For investigating the valence state changes of Mn, Fe, Co, Ni, and Cu in the Fe<sup>2+</sup>-C≡N-M<sup>2+</sup> group during electrochemical cycling, the normalized X-ray absorption near-edge spectroscopy (XANES) spectra at the Mn, Fe, Co, Ni, and Cu K-edges of the HE-K-PBA cathode with original, full charge and full discharge state were systematically analyzed as exhibited in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>g. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref13 ref42 ref54 ref57" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref13 ref42 ref54 ref57" aria-label="reference 13, 42, 54 and 57">(13,42,54,57)</a> Compared to the original state, the Mn, Fe and Co K-edge spectra shift to higher energy when charged to 4.2 V, and shift back to the original state at 2 V. However, the Ni K-edge spectrum does not shift during the whole charging and discharging process, indicating electrochemical inertia of Ni. And the Cu K-edge spectrum shows a similar process with Mn, Fe and Co during cycling process. The full discharge state spectrum of Cu shifts slightly to lower energy than its original state, possibly resulting from the reduction of a small amount of Cu<sup>2+</sup> to Cu<sup>+</sup>. In a word, the above results clarify that Mn, Fe, Co and Cu are electrochemically active and Fe<sup>2+</sup>/Fe<sup>3+</sup>, Mn<sup>2+</sup>/Mn<sup>3+</sup>, Co<sup>2+</sup>/Co<sup>3+</sup>, and Cu<sup>+</sup>/Cu<sup>2+</sup> are primarily responsible for the charge compensation mechanism in the Fe<sup>2+</sup>-C≡N-M<sup>2+</sup> group, while Ni<sup>2+</sup> acts as a stable frame element and does not participate in the reaction.</div><div class="NLM_p">To understand in depth  the reaction mechanism of each electrochemically active metal component (Mn, Fe, Co, Cu) in HE-K-PBA, <i>ex situ</i> XPS was examined on cathodes at pristine state and different charge/discharge voltage (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a> and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S31</a>). For the initial state of HE-K-PBA, the Mn and Fe cations predominantly exist in a divalent state. The Co cations present in a mixture of divalent and trivalent states, and the Cu cations exhibit a mixture of monovalent and divalent state, which may be attributed to the unavoidable oxidization during the preparation and testing process. To further get insight into the reaction mechanism of HE-K-PBA, XPS spectra at six voltages during the charging/discharging process were investigated (Charge (C) 3.2 V, C 3.4 V, C 4.2 V, and Discharge (D) 3.5 V, D 3.2 V, D 2 V). As shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>a, in the initial state, the peaks at 641.1  and 653.7 eV in the Mn 2p spectrum can be indexed to Mn 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and Mn 2p<sub>1/2</sub>, respectively, indicating that Mn exists in a divalent state. The peak close to 646 eV can be indexed as a shakeup satellite of Mn 2p peaks. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref37" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref37" aria-label="reference 37">(37)</a> The Mn 2p spectra show a significant shift between C 3.4 V, C 4.2 V, and D 3.5 V, while remaining constant between other voltage ranges. Thus, the reaction voltage of redox couples of Mn<sup>2+</sup> (641.1 eV)/Mn<sup>3+</sup> (643.1 eV) is in the voltage range of 3.5–4.2 V. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref48" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref48" aria-label="reference 48">(48)</a> <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>b shows the Fe 2p spectra during the charging and discharging process. In the initial sample, the peaks are mainly located at 708.8 eV (Fe 2p<sub>3/2</sub>) and 721.8 eV (Fe 2p<sub>1/2</sub>), indicating 2+ oxidation state of Fe. The peak shift occurs between initial and C 3.2 V (or reversible process, between D 3.2 V and D 2 V), representing the change from high spin Fe<sup>2+</sup> (708.8 eV) to Fe<sup>3+</sup> (709.9 eV) (Fe<sup>2+</sup>-C≡N–Fe<sup>2+</sup> → Fe<sup>2+</sup>-C≡N–Fe<sup>3+</sup>). The peak shift between C 3.4 V and C 4.2 V (or reversible process, between C 4.2 V and D 3.5 V) represents the change from low spin Fe<sup>2+</sup> to Fe<sup>3+</sup> (Fe<sup>2+</sup>-C≡N-M<sup>3+</sup> → Fe<sup>3+</sup>-C≡N-M<sup>3+</sup>). Thus, the reaction voltage of redox couples of Fe<sup>2+</sup>/Fe<sup>3+</sup> mainly occurs in two voltage ranges, 2–3.2 V, and 3.5–4.2 V, representing the change of high and low spin Fe, respectively. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26 ref45" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref26 ref45" aria-label="reference 26 and 45">(26,45)</a> The XPS spectra of Co 2p are shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>c. In the initial state, the peaks of Co 2p<sub>3/2</sub> are mainly located at 781.3 and 784.8 eV, and peaks of Co 2p<sub>1/2</sub> are located at 795.7 and 797.6 eV, which indicate the presence of Co<sup>3+</sup> and Co<sup>2+</sup>, respectively. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref44" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref44" aria-label="reference 44">(44)</a> The peak close to 788 eV can be indexed as a shakeup satellite of Co 2p peaks. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref37" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref37" aria-label="reference 37">(37)</a> It can be found that the peak change of Co 2p occurs throughout the whole voltage ranges, and the main change occurs between C 3.2  and C 3.4 V (or reversible process, D 3.5–D 3.2 V). From C 3.2 V to C 3.4 V, the peak of Co<sup>3+</sup> is significantly enhanced, and the peak of Co<sup>2+</sup> is correspondingly weakened, indicating the transition from Co<sup>2+</sup> to Co<sup>3+</sup>. However, in the other voltage ranges, the valence of Co changes slowly. It can be judged that the redox couples of Co<sup>2+</sup>/Co<sup>3+</sup> mainly occurs between 3.2 and 3.4 V. As for the Cu 2p spectra (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>d), a similar process could be found with Co 2p. The peaks of Cu 2p<sub>3/2</sub> are located at 932.5 and 935.3 eV, and the peaks of Cu 2p<sub>1/2</sub> are located at 952.7 and 955.0 eV, indicating the presence of Cu<sup>+</sup> and Cu<sup>2+</sup> in the initial state, respectively, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref26" aria-label="reference 26">(26)</a> illustrating that an internal redox reaction from Cu<sup>2+</sup> to Cu<sup>+</sup> occurred during the HE-K-PBA synthesis process. Even so, the average oxidation state of nitrogen-coordinated M (Mn, Fe, Co, Ni, Cu) cations is divalent, which is consistent with the expected PBA structure of Fe<sup>2+</sup>-C≡N-M<sup>2+</sup>. The peak located at 928.8 eV can be indexed as the Cu<sup>2+</sup> for Cu–O (Cu with coordinate water). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref26" aria-label="reference 26">(26)</a> The peak close to 943 eV can be indexed as a shakeup satellite of Cu 2p peaks. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref37" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref37" aria-label="reference 37">(37)</a> The change of copper valence state lasts throughout the electrochemical process and mainly occurs in the voltage range between initial and C 3.4 V (or reversible process, D 3.5–D 2 V). Compared with the initial state, when charged to 3.4 V, the signal of Cu<sup>+</sup> is obviously weakened, accompanied by the signal of Cu<sup>2+</sup> significantly enhanced. In addition, for these four electrochemical active elements (Mn, Fe, Co, Cu), the spectra of the fully discharged state (D 2 V)  exactly correspond with the initial state, indicating a high reversibility reaction of HE-K-PBA. And the results are fully consistent with the above XANES characterization.</div><figure id="fig4" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/asset/images/medium/nn3c02323_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/asset/images/large/nn3c02323_0004.jpeg" id="gr4" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. <i>Ex situ</i> XPS analysis of each electrochemically active metal component: (a) Mn, (b) Fe, (c) Co, (d) Cu at initial, C 3.2 V, C 3.4 V, C 4.2 V, D 3.5 V, D 3.2 V, and D 2 V states from HE-K-PBA electrodes.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/asset/images/large/nn3c02323_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.3c02323&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">It should be noted that the stable structure of cathode materials is imperative for realizing superior electrochemical performance. Thus, the <i>in situ</i> XRD was carried out to investigate the structure evolution of HE-K-PBA cathode during the charge/discharge process. As shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>a, the electrochemical phase reversibility of HE-K-PBA is good through a complete electrochemical cycle, which accounts for the good electrochemical performance of the HE-K-PBA cathode. A phase appears at the high voltage region, which can be indexed to the cubic phase, and the cubic phase completely disappears at the full discharge state. Additionally, the finite element simulation is applied to elucidate the entropy stabilization mechanism of cathode structure. The volume change of HE-K-PBA during the discharge process is simulated by thermal expansion. In <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>b and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S5</a>, the average strain of the HE-K-PBA is much smaller than that of Mn-K-PBA and the other four single component PBAs (Co-K-PBA, Ni-K-PBA, Cu-K-PBA and Fe-K-PBA). The results show that the high entropy effect can effectively suppress the volume change during the electrochemical cycle, which can distinctly enhance the structural stability of electrode. The lower average strain of HE-K-PBA means that the expansion of materials is limited, which mainly origins from the interaction among these five metal components. Furthermore, under the same load and constraint conditions, both the maximum and minimum von Mises stress of HE-K-PBA are significantly lower than those of Mn-K-PBA and the other four single component PBAs (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>c and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S32</a>). The detailed values are exhibited in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>d and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S5</a>. It should be noted that the stress distribution of five single component PBAs is similar, which is obviously different from that of HE-K-PBA. The stress–concentration caused by external factors will be weakened because of the high entropy effect. Generally, failure of materials generally occurs at the position of maximum stress. The smaller maximum von Mises stress in the HE-K-PBA could prevent the active material from breaking and falling off due to the volume expansion. Furthermore, the difference between the maximum and minimum von Mises stress of HE-K-PBA and other five single compound PBAs are compared and applied in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>e. It is clear that HE-K-PBA exhibits the smallest stress difference, indicating that the high entropy effect could homogenize the internal stress inside the materials. To more intuitively demonstrate the structural stability of HE-K-PBA, post-mortem scanning electron microscopy (SEM) (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S33 and S35</a>) and TEM analysis (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S34 and S36</a>) were conducted. Apparently, the grain of HE-K-PBA still maintains regularity (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S33 and S34</a>), but the grain of Mn-K-PBA is obviously broken, and the edge is irregular after 100 cycles. This shows that the structural stability of HE-K-PBA is better than that of Mn-K-PBA during the electrochemical cycles. Benefiting from the distinctive high entropy effect, the HE-K-PBA shows superior structure stability which can effectively restrain electrode structure distortion and ensure the long cycle stability of HE-K-PBA cathode. Density functional theory (DFT) calculations were carried out to obtain the advantage of HE-K-PBA at the atomic scale (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S37</a>). Compared with the band gap of Mn-K-PBA, the band gap of HE-K-PBA is much lower, indicating that the distinctive high entropy effect can significantly improve the electronic conductivity.</div><figure id="fig5" data-index="5" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 5</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/asset/images/medium/nn3c02323_0005.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/asset/images/large/nn3c02323_0005.jpeg" id="gr5" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 5. (a) <i>In situ</i> XRD patterns of HE-K-PBA during the first cycle and corresponding charge/discharge curves. (b) Distributions of strain of HE-K-PBA and Mn-K-PBA. (c) Three-dimensional von Mises stress distributions and corresponding ground stress distributions of HE-K-PBA and Mn-K-PBA. (d) The maximum and minimum von Mises stress and (e) the difference between maximum and minimum von Mises stress of HE-K-PBA, Mn-K-PBA, Co-K-PBA, Ni-K-PBA, Cu-K-PBA, and Fe-K-PBA.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/asset/images/large/nn3c02323_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.3c02323&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">To evaluate the potential application of the HE-K-PBA cathode, a full-cell assembled with the HE-K-PBA cathode and hard carbon anode (denoted as HE-K-PBA||hard carbon) was configured, as illustrated in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>a. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>b exhibits the voltage–capacity profiles for the first three cycles at 1.0 A g<sup>–1</sup> within the voltage window of 2.0–3.9 V. The HE-K-PBA || hard carbon full cell presents satisfactory rate capacities of 273.4, 236.4, 206.2, 186.5, 171.4, 148.7, and 117.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.2, 0.5, 1.0, 1.5, 2.0, 2.5, and 3.0 A g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>c) (based on the mass of hard carbon). <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>d shows good cyclic stability of the HE-K-PBA || hard carbon full cell over 200 cycles at 1.0 A g<sup>–1</sup> and high retention of 82.7% as 182.4 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> during the 200th cycle. Moreover, it can power a light-emitting diode (LED) array logo of “Yu Lab” (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>e), demonstrating practical application of the constructed pouch cells. The performance comparison  with other previously reported full cells is shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S38</a>. To further demonstrate the wider compatibility in energy storage systems, the HE-K-PBA was investigated as the cathode for all-solid-state battery (ASSBs) matched with conventional PEO-based solid polymer electrolyte. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref58 ref59 ref60" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref58 ref59 ref60" aria-label="reference 58 to 60">(58−60)</a> The assembly structure of ASSBs is illustrated in  <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>f. The voltage–capacity profiles for the first five cycles at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup> within a voltage window of 2.5–4.0 V are shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>g. In order to demonstrate the validity of voltage lifting effect in the ASSB system, the long-term median voltage performance of HE-K-PBA at a current density of 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup> is shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>h. Apparently, the HE-K-PBA can provide a stable median voltage of 3.29 V over 3000 cycles. Moreover, the ASSB in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>i displays impressive cyclic stability with a good capacity retention rate of 80.0% over 3000 cycles. The electrochemical performances of HE-K-PBA in the full cell and all-solid-state battery further confirm the highly promising candidate for large-scale applications.</div><figure id="fig6" data-index="6" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 6</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/asset/images/medium/nn3c02323_0006.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/asset/images/large/nn3c02323_0006.jpeg" id="gr6" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 6. (a) An illustration of the structure of the HE-K-PBA || Hard carbon full cell. (b) The voltage–capacity profiles for the first three cycles at 1.0 A g<sup>–1</sup>. (c) Rate performance and (d) cycling performance at 1.0 A g<sup>–1</sup> of the HE-K-PBA || Hard carbon full cell. (e) Digital photos of lighting LED using pouch cell. (f) An illustration of the structure of ASSBs with PEO-based solid electrolyte. (g) Voltage–capacity profiles for the first five cycles at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup> of ASSBs. (h) Long-term median voltage performance and (i) long-term cycling performance at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup> of ASSBs.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/asset/images/large/nn3c02323_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.3c02323&amp;id=fig6"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div><div id="sec3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i3">Conclusions</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">In summary, we developed an advanced K<sub><i>x</i></sub>(MnFeCoNiCu)[Fe(CN)<sub>6</sub>] cathode (HE-K-PBA) with superior structure stability and high output voltage via the high-entropy and potassium incorporation strategy for SIBs. The obtained HE-K-PBA cathode delivers high reversible capacity (120.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>) and energy density (400.4 Wh kg<sup>–1</sup>) with a stable discharge voltage around 3.46 V. Even at a high current density of 1.0 A g<sup>–1</sup>, the HE-K-PBA cathode can still embody good cycling stability with a considerable capacity retention of 90.4% over 1700 cycles due to the stable high entropy framework. The highly competitive performances of assembled Na ion full cells and all-solid-state Na ion batteries further demonstrate the good application prospects of the HE-K-PBA cathode. Besides, the everlasting K<sup>+</sup> (de)intercalation mechanism in HE-K-PBA lattice without K<sup>+</sup> replacement with Na<sup>+</sup> is confirmed by postcyclic XRD, XPS, and TOF-SIMS, which strongly demonstrates the long-term effectiveness of enhanced working voltage. And <i>in situ</i> Raman, <i>ex situ</i> XANES and <i>ex situ</i> XPS are combined to deepen the understanding of the valence state changes of five high entropy elements. We also reveal the entropy stabilization mechanism of HE-K-PBA structure through the finite element simulation, demonstrating the low strain and stress–concentration in HE-K-PBA may effectively restrain structural distortion and damage. Our strategies of high-entropy and potassium incorporation can shed lights on constructing advanced cathode materials for SIBs with conspicuous cycling stability and high energy density.</div></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i4">Experimental Section</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec4_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i5" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i5"> Synthesis of HE-K-PBA and Mn-K-PBA Samples</h3><div class="NLM_p last">High-entropy Prussian blue analogue K<sub>1.29</sub>(MnFeCoNiCu)[Fe(CN)<sub>6</sub>] (HE-K-PBA) was synthesized by a conventional coprecipitation method under room temperature. In detail, 2.5 mmol of K<sub>4</sub>Fe(CN)<sub>6</sub> and 0.25 mmol of EDTA-2K·2H<sub>2</sub>O were dissolved in 50 mL deionized water to create solution A; 0.5 mmol FeSO<sub>4</sub>, 0.5 mmol MnSO<sub>4</sub>, 0.5 mmol CoSO<sub>4</sub>, 0.5 mmol NiSO<sub>4</sub>, and 0.5 mmol CuSO<sub>4</sub> were dissolved in 50 mL of deionized water to create solution B. And then, solution B was slowly dropwise added into solution A under continuous magnetic stirring and N<sub>2</sub> bubbling to form solution C. After aging for 24 h, the precipitate was obtained by centrifugation and washed with deionized water for several times, and dried under vacuum at 120 °C for 10 h. The obtained samples were marked as HE-K-PBA. As a comparison, Mn-K-PBA samples were synthesized analogously by using only MnSO<sub>4</sub> in solution B.</div></div><div id="sec4_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i6" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i6"> Material Characterization</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The crystal structures of HE-K-PBA and Mn-K-PBA were tested by X-ray diffraction (XRD) (Rigaku SmartLab) with a Cu Kα source. The morphologies and structures of HE-K-PBA and Mn-K-PBA were characterized via  transmission electron microscopy (JEM-2100F, JEOL Ltd., Tokyo, Japan). The bonding information was tested by X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS). The Raman spectroscopy was performed by a Renishaw in Via-Reflex Raman Microscope. The Mn, Fe, Co, Ni and Cu K-edge XAS spectra were measured in fluorescence mode at the 7-BM beamline (QAS) of National Synchrotron Light Source II (NSLS II), Brookhaven National Laboratory (BNL). The data was analyzed using the Athena software. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref61" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref61" aria-label="reference 61">(61)</a> The microstructure and morphology of the samples were examined by scanning electron microscopy (SEM) (JSM-6700, JEOL, Japan) and transmission electron microscopy (JEM-2100F, JEOL, Japan). The H<sub>2</sub>O contents of the synthetic material were analyzed by TGA (Q 600SDT) in an Ar atmosphere. The time-of-flight secondary ion mass spectrometry (TOF-SIMS5–100) was equipped with a 5 kV Bi<sup>+</sup> ions analysis beam and 1 kV Cs<sup>+</sup> sputtering for detecting negative secondary-ion fragments.</div></div><div id="sec4_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i7" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i7"> Electrochemical Characterizations</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The HE-K-PBA electrodes were fabricated by mixing the active materials (HE-K-PBA), carbon black, and polytetrafluoroethylene with a mass ratio of 7:2:1 onto the carbon coated Al foil. Then the thin film was dried at 120 °C in a vacuum oven overnight. The hard carbon electrodes were fabricated by mixing 70 wt % hard carbon, 20 wt % carbon black, and 10 wt % carboxymethyl cellulose (CMC). The mixed slurry was coated onto an Al foil and then dried at 60 °C overnight. The loading mass of HE-K-PBA and hard carbon on the electrodes were 1–2 and 1–1.5 mg cm<sup>–2</sup>, respectively. Sodium metal foils and glass fiber were used as the counter electrodes and separators, respectively. The electrolyte was 1 M NaClO<sub>4</sub> in propylene carbonate with a 5% fluoroethylene carbonate additive. Coin cells (2032-type) were assembled in an argon-filled glovebox with O<sub>2</sub> and H<sub>2</sub>O concentrations less than 0.1 ppm. The cycling and rate performances were examined on a Neware battery cycler (BTS BTS-610, Shenzhen, China) with a voltage range of 2.0–4.2 V. CHI660D electrochemical workstation was used for cyclic voltammetry (CV) at different scan rates from 2.0 to 4.2 V. For the preparation of HE-Na-PBA electrodes, an electrochemical method was used. First, charge the HE-K-PBA electrode to 4.2 V to remove all the K<sup>+</sup> from the HE-K-PBA electrode. Then  the cell was disassembled and reassemble it. The reassembled cell was discharged to 2.0 V to insert Na<sup>+</sup> into the initial lattice to obtain the HE-Na-PBA electrode. For the Full cell assembly, to eliminate the irreversible capacity of the hard carbon anode, the hard carbon was precycled five cycles with a voltage window of 0.01 to 2.0 V (vs K<sup>+</sup>/K) in the hard carbon || Na metal cell and then charge to 2.0 V. To assemble the full cell, the mass ratio of HE-K-PBA: hard carbon is 1:0.5. The specific capacities of full cells were calculated based on the mass of anode materials. The charge/discharge tests were conducted with the voltage range of 2.0–3.9 V. EIS test was carried on the Autolab PGSTAT 302N workstation with an AC voltage of 5 mV amplitude in the frequency ranging from 100 kHz to 10mHz. Solid-state batteries were fabricated using HE-K-PBA cathode, Na metal anode and conventional PEO-based solid electrolyte. Charge–discharge cycles of HE-K-PBA/PEO/Na all solid-state batteries were tested on a Landing testing instrument within a voltage range of 2.5–4.0 V (vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na) at a temperature of 60 °C.</div></div><div id="sec4_4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i8" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i8"> Calculation of Ion Diffusion Coefficient</h3><div class="NLM_p">The ion diffusion coefficient was calculated via the Randles-Sevcik equation: <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref62" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref62" aria-label="reference 62">(62)</a><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eqS1"><div class="equation"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"><span class="MJXp-math MJXp-display" id="MJXp-Span-1"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-2"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-3"><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-4"><span class="MJXp-msub" id="MJXp-Span-5"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-6" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-7">I</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-8" id="MJXp-Span-11" style="margin-left: 0.333em; margin-right: 0.333em;">=</span><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-12"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-13">2.68</span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-14" style="margin-left: 0.03em; margin-right: 0.03em;">·</span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-15"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-16" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span id="MJXp-Span-19">5</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-20"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-21" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-22">n</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-23" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-24">2</span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-25">/</span><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-26">3</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-27">A</span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-28"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-29" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-30">D</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-31" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-32">1</span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-33">/</span><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-34">2</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-35">C</span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-36"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-37" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-38">ω</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-39" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-40">1</span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-41">/</span><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-42">2</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><script type="math/mml" id="MathJax-Element-1"><math display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msub><mrow><mi>I</mi></mrow><mrow><mi>p</mi></mrow></msub></mstyle></mrow></mrow><mrow><mo linebreak="nobreak">=</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mn>2.68</mn><mo lspace="0.03em" rspace="0.03em">·</mo><msup><mrow><mn>10</mn></mrow><mrow><mn>5</mn></mrow></msup><msup><mrow><mi>n</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn><mo>/</mo><mn>3</mn></mrow></msup><mi>A</mi><msup><mrow><mi>D</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>/</mo><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup><mi>C</mi><msup><mrow><mi>ω</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>/</mo><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup></mstyle></mrow></math></script></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(1)</span></div></div></div><div class="NLM_p last">In the equation, <i>I</i><sub>p</sub> represents the maximal current, <i>n</i> represents the number of involved electrons in the reaction, <i>A</i> represents the area between the electrolyte and electrode, <i>D</i> represents the ion diffusion coefficient, <i>C</i> represents the molar concentration of Na<sup>+</sup> in PBA, and ω is the scan rate. The corresponding values are applied in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S4</a>.</div></div><div id="sec4_5" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i10" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i10"> Finite element simulation</h3><div class="NLM_p last">Thermomechanical coupling modules in the Finite element simulations were carried out to simulate the volume deformation of electrodes during the discharge process. The elastic modulus, Poisson’s ratio, and density of the material were shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.3c02323/suppl_file/nn3c02323_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S6</a>. A global displacement boundary condition is set at the center of the entire structure, and the displacement in three directions is zero. The entire structure is set with an overall heat flux heat load, with a body heat flux of 500 000 mW m<sup>2</sup>. The defined contact pair consists of a master surface and a slave surface. In the contact simulation, the contact direction is the normal direction of the master surface. Nodes on the slave surface will not cross the master surface, but points on the master surface can cross the slave surface. There is only a small relative slip between the two contact surfaces, and the magnitude of the slip is only a small part of the element size. During the entire analysis process, the contact relationship will not change. The solid mechanical modules were conducted to investigate the von Mises stress distribution of different samples by using COMSOL. The boundary conditions were applied with the same fixed constraint condition. The boundary load condition of all models is the same as 1 MPa.</div></div><div id="sec4_6" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i11" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i11"> First-Principle Calculations</h3><div class="NLM_p last">First-principle calculations were performed by employing the Vienna ab initio simulation package (VASP) software. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref63" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref63" aria-label="reference 63">(63)</a> The generalized gradient approximation (GGA) <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref64" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref64" aria-label="reference 64">(64)</a> with Perdew–Burke–Ernzerhof (PBE) <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref65" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref65" aria-label="reference 65">(65)</a> exchange-correlation Functions were adopted with the plane-wave cutoff energy set at 500 eV for all computations. The DFT+U method <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref66" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref66" aria-label="reference 66">(66)</a> were used to the transition metal of Mn, Fe, Co, Ni, Cu and the values of U were set to be 5.0, 4.3, 5.7, 6.0, and 4.0 eV, respectively. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref67" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref67" aria-label="reference 67">(67)</a> For the relaxations of the model structures, the energy and forces convergence criteria were set as 10<sup>–5</sup> eV and 0.03 eV Å<sup>–1</sup>, respectively. For the electronic structure calculations, the K-point mesh was set to be 2 × 3 × 4.</div></div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes-2"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i12">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">.                 10.1126/science.aay9972</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D370%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D708-711%26journal%3DScience%26issue%3D6517%26author%3DC.%2BZhao%26author%3DQ.%2BWang%26author%3DZ.%2BYao%26author%3DJ.%2BWang%26author%3DB.%2BSanchez-Lengeling%26author%3DF.%2BDing%26author%3DX.%2BQi%26author%3DY.%2BLu%26author%3DX.%2BBai%26author%3DB.%2BLi%26title%3DRational%2Bdesign%2Bof%2Blayered%2Boxide%2Bmaterials%2Bfor%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1126%252Fscience.aay9972&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.3c02323&amp;doiOfLink=10.1126%2Fscience.aay9972&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rational design of layered oxide materials for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Chenglong; Wang, Qidi; Yao, Zhenpeng; Wang, Jianlin; Sanchez-Lengeling, Benjamin; Ding, Feixiang; Qi, Xingguo; Lu, Yaxiang; Bai, Xuedong; Li, Baohua; Li, Hong; Aspuru-Guzik, Alan; Huang, Xuejie; Delmas, Claude; Wagemaker, Marnix; Chen, Liquan; Hu, Yong-Sheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Science (Washington, DC, United States)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">370</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6517</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">708-711</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SCIEAS</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1095-9203</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Association for the Advancement of Science</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries have captured widespread attention for grid-scale energy storage owing to the natural abundance of sodium.  The performance of such batteries is limited by available electrode materials, esp. for sodium-ion layered oxides, motivating the exploration of high compositional diversity.  How the compn. dets. the structural chem. is decisive for the electrochem. performance but very challenging to predict, esp. for complex compns.  The "cationic potential" is introduced that captures the key interactions of layered materials and makes it possible to predict the stacking structures.  This is demonstrated through the rational design and prepn. of layered electrode materials with improved performance.  As the stacking structure dets. the functional properties, this methodol. offers a soln. toward the design of alkali metal layered oxides.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref4" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1021/cr500192f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yabuuchi, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kubota, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dahbi, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Komaba, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Research development on sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Prussian blue analogs cathodes for aqueous zinc ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yuanxia; Zhao, Jingxin; Hu, Qiang; Hao, Tianwei; Cao, Heng; Huang, Xiaomin; Liu, Yu; Zhang, Yanyan; Lin, Dunmin; Tang, Yuxin; Cai, Yongqing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Today Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Aq. zinc ion batteries (AZIBs) with high theor. capacity, low cost, and highly safety that have been considered as one of the most promising candidates for the next generation of electrochem. energy storage applications.  However, the hydrated zinc ions have strong electrostatic force with the host material, causing the low output voltage and poor reversibility.  Thus, exploiting suitable cathode materials with high voltage, specific capacity, and stable cycling performance is still a challenge.  Recently, the development of cathode materials mainly focuses on manganese-based, vanadium-based, org., and Prussian blue analog (PBAs) materials.  Among these cathodes' materials, PBAs have attracted great attention for AZIBs owing to their high working voltage, tunable chem. compn. and microstructure, open 3D frameworks, low cost, and ease of synthesis.  To record the recent rapid development PBAs materials toward high-performance AZIBs, we provide fundamental insights into the structure characteristics and synthesis control of PBAs and present an overview of recent developments of PBAs as promising cathodes for AZIBs.  Finally, the key challenges and future opportunities in this rapidly developing field are also presented in this review.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref6" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1002/cssc.202200564"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Fast Intercalation of Lithium in Semi-Metallic γ-GeSe Nanosheet: A New Group-IV Monochalcogenide for Lithium-Ion Battery Application</span>. <i>ChemSusChem</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>15</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">e202200564</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
